<ul><li><a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_in_England" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in England">LDS Church in England</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Britain_Yearly_Meeting" title="Britain Yearly Meeting">Quakers</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a></li></ul></div></div></td>
</tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Methodist Church participates in various ecumenical forums and interdenominational associations. The church is a member of the three national ecumenical bodies in Great Britain, namely <a href="/wiki/Churches_Together_in_England" title="Churches Together in England">Churches Together in England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyt%C3%BBn" title="Cytûn">Cytûn</a> in Wales and <a href="/wiki/Action_of_Churches_Together_in_Scotland" title="Action of Churches Together in Scotland">Action of Churches Together in Scotland</a>, plus <a href="/wiki/Churches_Together_in_Britain_and_Ireland" title="Churches Together in Britain and Ireland">Churches Together in Britain and Ireland</a>. It also participates in the <a href="/wiki/Conference_of_European_Churches" title="Conference of European Churches">Conference of European Churches</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Council_of_Churches" title="World Council of Churches">World Council of Churches</a>. The church has sent delegates to every Assembly of the World Council and has at various times been represented on its Central Committees and Faith and Order Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Methodist Church is officially committed to "seek opportunities to work in partnership with other denominations" and "seek opportunities to join with other Christians in sharing the Good News of the Gospel and to make more followers of Jesus Christ through together bearing witness to the unity of the one, holy, catholic and apostolic Church."<sup id="cite_ref-Vision_Statement_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vision_Statement-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> From the 1970s onward, the Methodist Church has been involved in over 900 <a href="/wiki/Local_ecumenical_partnership" title="Local ecumenical partnership">local ecumenical partnerships</a> (LEPs) with neighbouring denominations,<sup id="cite_ref-WCC-MCOGB_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCC-MCOGB-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> such as the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baptist_Union_of_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist Union of Great Britain">Baptist Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Reformed_Church" title="United Reformed Church">United Reformed Church</a>. The Methodist Church is also one of the <a href="/wiki/Covenanted_Churches_in_Wales" title="Covenanted Churches in Wales">Covenanted Churches in Wales</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Church_in_Wales" title="Church in Wales">Church in Wales</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_Wales" title="Presbyterian Church of Wales">Presbyterian Church of Wales</a>, the United Reformed Church and certain <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> churches.<sup id="cite_ref-Wales_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wales-200">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2016 the World Methodist Council opened an Ecumenical Office in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, Italy. Methodist leaders and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> met together to dedicate the new office.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> It exists to offer a resource in the city of Rome for the global Methodist family and to help facilitate Methodist relationships with the wider <a href="/wiki/Christian_Church" title="Christian Church">Christian Church</a>, especially the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Anglican.E2.80.93Methodist_Covenant"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglican–Methodist_Covenant">Anglican–Methodist Covenant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Anglican–Methodist Covenant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1960s, the Methodist Church made ecumenical overtures to the Church of England, aimed at church unity.<sup id="cite_ref-common_statement_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-common_statement-203">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> In February 1963, a report, <i>Conversations between the Church of England and the Methodist Church</i>, was published. This gave an outline of a scheme to unite the two churches. The scheme was not without opposition, for four Methodist representatives; <a href="/wiki/C._K._Barrett" title="C. K. Barrett">Kingsley Barrett</a>, Meadley, Snaith and Jessop, issued a dissentient report.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Through much of the 1960s, controversy spread in the two churches. Central in the debate was the need for Methodist ministers to be ordained under the Anglican <a href="/wiki/Historical_episcopate" title="Historical episcopate">historical episcopate</a>, which opponents characterised as "<a href="/wiki/Reordination" title="Reordination">reordination</a>" of Methodist ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-common_statement_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-common_statement-203">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Discussions failed when the proposals for union were rejected by the Church of England's <a href="/wiki/General_Synod_of_the_Church_of_England" title="General Synod of the Church of England">General Synod</a> in 1972 but were renewed in the mid-1990s, with a series of Informal Conversations held in 1995 and 1996. These meetings concluded with the publication of a common statement in December 2000 which highlighted common beliefs and potential areas of cooperation between the two denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-common_statement_203-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-common_statement-203">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2002, the British Methodist Conference voted on the proposals in <i>An Anglican–Methodist Covenant</i>, sending it to its districts for discussion. On 1 November 2003, in the presence of Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, the president and other leaders of the Methodist Conference and the leaders of the Church of England signed the covenant at <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Central_Hall,_Westminster" title="Methodist Central Hall, Westminster">Methodist Central Hall</a> in Westminster.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The covenant affirms the willingness of the two churches to work together at a diocesan/district level in matters of <a href="/wiki/Evangelism" title="Evangelism">evangelism</a> and joint worship.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/English_Covenant" title="English Covenant">English Covenant</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_over_report_on_Zionism">Controversy over report on Zionism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Controversy over report on Zionism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the submission of a report entitled <i>Justice for Palestine and Israel</i> in July 2010, the British Methodist Conference was reported to have questioned whether "Zionism was compatible with Methodist beliefs".<sup id="cite_ref-meth2_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meth2-207">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-meth3_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meth3-208">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christian_Zionism" title="Christian Zionism">Christian Zionism</a> was broadly characterised as believing that Israel "must be held above criticism whatever policy is enacted", and Conference called for a boycott of selected goods from <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">Israeli settlements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-meth_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meth-209">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chief_Rabbis_of_the_United_Hebrew_Congregations" title="List of Chief Rabbis of the United Hebrew Congregations">Chief Rabbi</a> of Britain's <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Jewish">Orthodox Jewish</a> community described the report as "unbalanced, factually and historically flawed" and charged that it offered "no genuine understanding of one of the most complex conflicts in the world today. Many in both communities will be deeply disturbed."<sup id="cite_ref-meth2_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meth2-207">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-meth3_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meth3-208">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide_Methodism">Worldwide Methodism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Worldwide Methodism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Methodist_denominations" title="List of Methodist denominations">List of Methodist denominations</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Scots_Church,_Malta" title="St. Andrew&#39;s Scots Church, Malta">St Andrew's Scots Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, is a joint congregation of the Methodist Church of Great Britain and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> situated in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> There are also Methodist congregations in the <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and the Channel Islands (each forming a district).<sup id="cite_ref-Stats1_182-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stats1-182">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Methodist churches in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> are part of the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_in_Ireland" title="Methodist Church in Ireland">Methodist Church in Ireland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> a separate Connexion which is historically associated with the British Methodist Church.
</p><p>Methodism is a worldwide movement with around 80.5 million adherents (including members of <a href="/wiki/United_and_uniting_churches" title="United and uniting churches">united and uniting churches</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-WMCAbout_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMCAbout-212">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Its largest denomination is the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> which has congregations on four continents (though the majority are in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Almost all Methodist denominations meet together <a href="/wiki/Quinquennial" class="mw-redirect" title="Quinquennial">quinquennially</a> in a conference of the <a href="/wiki/World_Methodist_Council" title="World Methodist Council">World Methodist Council</a>, with its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Junaluska,_North_Carolina" title="Lake Junaluska, North Carolina">Lake Junaluska, North Carolina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WMCAbout_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMCAbout-212">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pronounced as <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="/θ/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thigh&#39;">θ</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the 18th century "enthusiasm" was a British pejorative term for advocacy of any political or religious cause in public, i.e. <a href="/wiki/Fanaticism" title="Fanaticism">fanaticism</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-151"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-151">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This restriction no longer applies to domestic occasions in private homes, i.e. the minister may have a drink at home in the <a href="/wiki/Manse" title="Manse">manse</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-162"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-162">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Both titles are found in various places in the <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a>. The word "presbyter" derives from <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <i>πρεσβύτερος</i> (<i>presbyteros</i>), the comparative form of <i>πρέσβυς</i> (<i>presbus</i>), "elder".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The word "deacon" derives from <i>διάκονος</i> (<i>diakonos</i>), a standard ancient Greek word which had a variety of meanings centred around service, message and attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Jr, Charles Yrigoyen (25 September 2014). <i>T&amp;T Clark Companion to Methodism</i>.
